time of this codification ____________ jay jaxon jr mayor ____________ h collis perdue president e m white president pro tempore johnny a knight robert l mccullar jr will price city council ____________ jimmy s calton city attorney ____________ linda w howell cmc city clerktreasurer preface this a complete recodification of the general and permanent ordinances of the city of eufaula alabama source materials used in the preparation of the the 1974 as supplemented  and ordinances subsequently adopted by the council the source of each section is included in the history note appearing in parentheses at the end thereof the absence of such a note indicates that the section is new and was adopted for the first time with the adoption of the use of the comparative tables appearing in the back of this the reader can locate any section of the 1974 as supplemented and any subsequent ordinance included herein the chapters of the been conveniently arranged in alphabetical order and the various sections within each chapter have been catchlined to facilitate usage notes which tie related sections of the which refer to relevant state law have been included a table listing the state law citations and setting forth their location within the included at the back of this system the chapter and section numbering system used in this the same system used in many state and local government codes each section number consists of two parts separated by a dash the figure before the dash refers to the chapter number and the figure after the dash refers to the position of the section within the chapter thus the second section of chapter 1 is numbered 12 and the first section of chapter 6 is 61 under this system each section is identified with its chapter and at the same time new sections or even whole chapters can be inserted in their proper place by using the decimal system for amendments for example if new material consisting of one section that would logically come between sections 101 and 102 is desired to be added such new section would be numbered 1015 new chapters may be included by using one of the reserved chapter numbers care should be taken that the alphabetical arrangement of chapters is maintained when including new chapters new articles and new divisions may be included in the same way or in the case of articles may be placed at the end of the chapter embracing the subject and in the case of divisions may be placed at the end of the article embracing the subject the next successive number shall be assigned to the new article or division page numbering system the page numbering system used in this a prefix system the letters to the left of the colon are an abbreviation which represents a certain portion of the volume the number to the right of the colon represents the number of the page in that portion in the case of a chapter of the the number to the left of the colon indicates the number of the chapter code cd code comparative tables cct1 state law reference table slt1 code index cdi1 index the index has been prepared with the greatest of care each particular item has been placed under several headings some of which are couched in lay phraseology others in legal terminology and still others in language generally used by local government officials and employees there are numerous cross references within the index itself which stand as guideposts to direct the user to the particular item in which the user is interested looseleaf supplements a special feature of this publication is the looseleaf system of binding and supplemental servicing of the publication with this system the publication will be kept uptodate subsequent amendatory legislation will be properly edited and the appropriate page or pages affected will be reprinted these new pages will be distributed to holders of copies of the publication with instructions for the manner of inserting the new pages and deleting the obsolete pages keeping this publication uptodate at all times will depend largely upon the holder of the publication as revised sheets are received it will then become the responsibility of the holder to have the amendments inserted according to the attached instructions it is strongly recommended by the publisher that all such amendments be inserted immediately upon receipt to avoid misplacing them and in addition that all deleted pages be saved and filed for historical reference purposes acknowledgments this publication was under the direct supervision of roger d merriam supervising editor and jody wilson editor of the municipal tallahassee florida credit is gratefully given to the other members of the publishers staff for their sincere interest and able assistance throughout the project the publisher is most grateful to former mayor sam slade city attorney jimmy s calton and city clerktreasurer linda w howell cmc for their cooperation and assistance during the progress of the work on this publication it is hoped that their efforts and those of the publisher have resulted in a ordinances which will make the active law of the city readily accessible to all citizens and which will be a valuable tool in the daytoday administration of the citys affairs municipal code corporation tallahassee florida adopting ordinance ordinance no 19933 an enacting a new the city of eufaula alabama all ordinances of a general and permanent nature enacted on or before  and not included in the recognized and continued in force by reference therein are repealed the repeal provided for in hereof shall not be construed to revive any ordinance or part thereof that has been repealed by a subsequent ordinance that is repealed by this ordinance unless another penalty is expressly provided every person convicted of a violation of any provision of the any ordinance rule or regulation adopted or issued in pursuance thereof shall be punished by a fine not exceeding $50000 imprisonment not exceeding six months or any combination thereof each act of violation and each day upon which any such violation shall occur shall constitute a separate offense the penalty provided by this section unless another penalty is expressly provided shall apply to the amendment of any whether or not such penalty is reenacted in the amendatory ordinance in addition to the penalty prescribed above the city may pursue other remedies such as abatement of nuisances injunctive relief and revocation of licenses or permits additions or amendments to the passed in the form as to indicate the intention of the city council to make the same a part of the be deemed to be incorporated in the so that reference to the the additions and amendments ordinances adopted after  that amend or refer to ordinances that have been codified in the shall be construed as if they amend or refer to like provisions of the  this ordinance shall become effective immediately upon its passage and approval by the mayor or upon its otherwise becoming a law adopted and approved this 15th day of march 1993 city of eufaula alabama a municipal corporation s h collis perdue council president attest s linda w howell cmc city this and the following chapters and sections shall constitute and be designated the ordinances city of eufaula alabama and may be so cited  state law reference authority of city to provide for the revision and codification of its ordinances and for the adoption of a code ala 197  11457 rules of construction and definitions in the construction of this of all ordinances and resolutions passed by the city council the following rules of construction and definitions apply unless inconsistent with the manifest intent of the council or the context of the provisions generally the provisions of this be liberally construed to effect the purposes expressed therein or implied from the expression thereof in case of doubt or ambiguity in the meaning of such provisions the general shall yield to the particular interpretation and construction shall tend to further the accomplishment of the elimination of the particular mischiefs for which the provisions were enacted bond when a bond is required an undertaking in writing shall be required city city means the city of eufaula alabama city council council or city council means the city council of the city of eufaula constituting the governing body of the city city officers and departments whenever reference is made to an officer or a department the reference shall be construed as if followed by the words of the city of eufaula alabama reference to a specific officer shall include his authorized deputies agents and representatives means the ordinances eufaula alabama as designated in section 11 ala 1975 ala 1975 means the alabama 197 as amended computation of time in computing any period of time the day of the act event or default from which the designated period of time begins to run shall not be included the last day of the period so computed shall be included unless it is a saturday a sunday or a legal holiday in which event the period runs until the end of the next day which is not a saturday a sunday or a legal holiday when the period of time prescribed or allowed is less than seven days intermediate saturdays sundays and legal holidays shall be excluded in the computation county county means barbour county alabama gender a word importing the masculine gender only shall extend and be applied to females and to firms partnerships and corporations as well as to males joint authority words purporting to give authority to three or more officers or other persons shall be construed as giving such authority to a majority of such officers or other persons unless it is otherwise declared may may is to be construed as being permissive may not may not states a prohibition month month means a calendar month must must is to be construed as being mandatory number words used in the singular include the plural and the plural includes the singular oath oath is to be construed to include an affirmation in all cases in which by law an affirmation may be substituted for an oath and in such cases the words swear and sworn are equivalent to the words affirm and affirmed owner owner applied to a building or land includes any part owner joint owner tenant in common joint tenant or tenant by the entirety of the whole or of a part of such building or land person person includes a corporation a firm partnership association organization or any other group acting as a unit or its agent or assignee as well as a natural person personal property personal property includes every species of property except real property preceding following preceding and following mean next before and next after respectively property property includes real and personal property real property real property includes lands tenements and hereditaments shall shall is to be construed as being mandatory sidewalk sidewalk means a strip of land in front of or on the sides of a building or lot of land lying between the property line and the street signature or subscription signature or subscription includes a mark when the person cannot write state state means the state of alabama street street includes any street avenue boulevard road alley lane viaduct and other public ways in the city and all parts thereof within the designated rightofway technical and nontechnical words all words and phrases are to be construed and understood according to the common and approved usage of the language but technical words and phrases and such others as may have acquired a peculiar and appropriate meaning in the law are to be construed and understood according to such peculiar and appropriate meaning tense words used in the present or past tense include the future as well as the present and past writing writing or written includes printing on paper year year means a calendar year  state law reference definitions and rules of construction ala 197  111 112 catchlines of sections effect of history notes and references in a the catchlines of the sections of this in boldface type are intended as mere catchwords to indicate the contents of the sections and are not to be deemed or taken to be titles of such sections nor as any part of such sections nor unless expressly so provided are they to be so deemed when any of such sections including the catchlines are amended or reenacted b the history or source notes appearing in parentheses after sections in this not intended to have any legal effect but are merely intended to indicate the source of matter contained in the section cross references and state law references which appear after sections or subsections of this which otherwise appear in footnote form are provided for the convenience of the user of this have no legal effect c all references to chapters articles or sections are to the chapters articles and sections of this unless otherwise specified  police jurisdiction a this all ordinances of the city apply in the police jurisdiction of the city and to all property or rightsofway belonging to the city to the maximum extent authorized or required by ala 197  114010 115191 and other applicable law the use of the phrase in the city shall include the citys police jurisdiction and all such property and rightsofway b as provided in ala 197  114010 the police jurisdiction covers all adjoining territory within three miles of the corporate limits of the city  14 effect of repeal of ordinances a the repeal of an ordinance shall not revive any ordinances in force before or at the time the ordinance repealed took effect b the repeal of an ordinance shall not affect any punishment or penalty incurred before the repeal took effect nor any suit prosecution or proceeding pending at the time of the repeal for an offense committed or cause of action arising under the ordinance repealed  cross reference manner of repealing ordinances  238 general penalty  continuing violations a in this section the phrase violation of this  means 1 doing an act that is prohibited or made or declared unlawful an offense an offense against the city or a misdemeanor by ordinance or by rule or regulation authorized by ordinance  2 failure to perform an act that is required to be performed by ordinance or by rule or regulation authorized by ordinance  or 3 failure to perform an act if the failure is declared a misdemeanor an offense an offense against the city or unlawful by ordinance or by rule or regulation authorized by ordinance b in this section the phrase violation of this  does not include the failure of a city officer or city employee to perform an official duty unless it is provided that failure to perform the duty is to be punished as provided in this section c except as otherwise provided a person convicted of a violation of this be punished by a fine not exceeding $50000 imprisonment or confinement at hard labor for a term not exceeding six months or any combination thereof the penalty imposed upon a corporation shall consist of the fine only plus costs of court no penalty shall exceed the maximum established by state statute for the commission of a substantially similar offense for violations of this are continuous with respect to time each day the violation continues is a separate offense d the imposition of a penalty does not prevent revocation or suspension of a license permit or franchise e violations of this are continuous with respect to time may be abated by injunctive or other equitable relief the imposition of a penalty does not prevent equitable relief cross reference municipal court  3426 et seq  working out fines and costs  3441  court costs  3446 supplement or already embodied in the   provisions considered as continuations of existing ordinances the provisions appearing in this so far as they are the same in substance as those of ordinances be designated by the presiding officer will be applied if a situation is not covered in the preceding rules of procedure  10592   10796 vote required for altering amending or temporarily suspending rules the rules of the city council may be altered amended or temporarily suspended by a vote of twothirds of the members present  10592   10796 order of business the order of business at council meetings shall be as follows 1 call to order invocation roll call honors and recognition 2 approval of the agenda 3 consent agenda all items on the consent agenda have been distributed to each member of the city council for reading and study are considered to be routine and will be enacted by one motion of the city council with no separate discussion if separate discussion is desired that item may be removed from the consent agenda and placed on the regular agenda by request 4 report of mayor 5 visitors 6 ordinances and resolutions 7 public hearings 8 unfinished business 9 regular agenda new business 10 council actiondiscussion council committee reports 11 adjournment  10592     10796 permission required to speak more than twice no member of the city council shall speak more than twice on the same subject without permission of the presiding officer  10592   10796 permission required to address council no person not a member of the city council shall be allowed to address the city council while in session without permission of the presiding officer  10592   10796 city officers and employees to attend meetings on request all officers or employees of the city shall when requested attend all meetings of the city council and shall remain in the council room for such length of time as the council may direct  10592   10796 motions to reconsider motions to reconsider must be by a member of the city council who voted with the majority and at the same or next succeeding meeting of the city council  10592   10796 requests for recording of votes and division on questions whenever it shall be required by one or more members of the city council the yeas and nays shall be recorded  and any member may call for a division on any question  10592   10796 deciding questions of order all questions of order shall be decided by the presiding officer of the city council with the right of appeal to the city council by any member  10592   10796 presiding officers request for member to take chair the presiding officer of the city council may at his discretion call any member to take the chair to allow such presiding officer to address the city council make a motion or discuss any matter at issue  10592   10796 motions and questions first in order motions of the city council to lay any matter on the table shall be first in order and on all questions the last amendment the most distant day and the largest sum shall be put first  10592   10796 standing committees established the standing committees of the city council are established as follows 1 finance 2 inspection of books and papers of officers and agents every officer or agent of the city shall at reasonable times submit such officers or agents books and papers to the inspection of the city council or to any person or committee appointed or authorized by the council to examine the books and papers  delivery of materials to successor of officers and agents every officer or agent of the city on going out of office shall deliver over to his successor or to the city council as the case may require all books papers accounts tools instruments and everything pertaining to his office and shall be entitled to a receipt therefor if requested  defense and indemnification a definitions the following words terms and phrases when used in this section shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning employee includes all employees of the city whether classified or not or employees of any board appointed entirely by the mayor or city council excluding the board of education officer includes any elected or appointed official of the city or member of any board appointed entirely by the mayor or city council excluding the board of education b defense in actions among the duties of the city attorney shall be that of representing as counsel with the attorney fees and litigation fees being borne solely by the city any city officer or employee in connection with any claim suit for damages or other action against such person arising in connection with the performance by such officer or employee of his public duties such officer or employee may have his own counsel to assist in the defense at the expense of the officer or employee c indemnification any officer or employee who is held liable for the payment of any claims or damages by way of judgment or settlement shall be entitled to indemnification by the city where the acts resulting in such liability were done in good faith without malice within the scope of authority of the officer or employee any judgment rendered against an officer or employee whether for compensatory or punitive damages shall be presumed to have arisen from an act performed in good faith and without malice provided that the act was performed within the scope of authority and further provided that the city council does not find by resolution that the act was not performed in good faith or that the act was performed with malice this indemnification shall be secondary to any insurance coverage from any other source which covers the officer or employee for the same acts giving rise to the officers or employees liability no insurance company shall have any cause of action direct or indirect for reimbursement from the city for any expenses or judgments paid in covering such officer or employee for such acts d citys defenses nothing in this section shall be construed as waiving the citys defense of governmental immunity to it or its officers or employees in any action brought against the city or such officer or employee or to in any way expand upon the limitation of liability in state courts as set forth in the appropriate sections of state law e notice the provisions of this section shall apply only where the city has been given notice of any action brought against any city officer or employee based upon any action of such officer or employee within the scope of authority as such f conflict of interest nothing in this section or in any ordinance of the city and nothing in any agreement with the city attorney shall be construed to require the city attorney to provide legal services in any manner which would cause the attorney to be involved in a conflict of interest if the city attorney is not able to participate in the defense of an officer or superintendent of streets and sanitation shall have the following powers and perform the following duties 1 have the charge and control of the street working force of the city consisting of laborers trucks road machinery parts tools implements and equipment of all kinds for the cleaning repair and improvement of streets and handling of solid waste 2 devote his whole time and attention to the control and management of such department during working hours except when absent on the business of the office 3 apply that working force to the performance of such work of the city as directed by the committee on streets and sanitation 4 keep a correct account of all road machinery parts tools implements automobiles trucks equipment etc under his charge and any deficiency therein not accounted for shall be charged to him and deducted from his wages 5 cause to be removed all obstacles which he may find in the streets alleys sewers drains ditches sidewalks and pavements and if any person creating such obstruction or his agent shall fail or refuse to remove the obstacle the superintendent shall report such facts to the mayor 6 cause to be removed from the streets public alleys pavements and sidewalks all nuisances and shall report to the mayor the person causing such nuisance if known 7 report to the mayor and chief of police all persons who refuse to remove dead animals from their premises and if the owner of a dead animal is unknown the superintendent shall assist the chief of police in promptly removing the dead animal 8 have the power to hire all laborers necessary for conducting the affairs of the department subject to approval of the mayor 9 have the power to discharge any laborer who refuses to obey his orders and must immediately report the discharge to the mayor 10 see that all laborers employed by the street department discharge their duties and keep the time of all laborers employed by the department and report all time lost by such laborers to the mayor 11 have charge and control of all persons sentenced to hard labor on the streets of the city and see that they perform the labor required of them and that none escapes from his custody 12 see that due care is taken of all shade trees in or on the streets of the city and take such steps as are necessary to keep and preserve the trees it shall be his duty to set out additional trees whenever it is necessary 13 enforce all provisions of this to solid waste and to that end have the authority and power conferred by the provisions of this thereto 14 in addition serve as sanitation officer for the city and as such shall do and perform all such duties with regard to the enforcement of the provisions of this to health and sanitation as the council may direct 15 do all other things required of him by the mayor and the council  secs 22042215  reserved division 6  license inspector created there is created the office of license inspector for the city who shall hold filing of statement as to manner of injury and damages claims required prior to filing action for personal injuries against city see ala 197  1147192  secs 22992320  reserved article vi  capital assets intent it is the intent of the city council to establish a uniform system of accountability to safeguard the citys considerable investment in capital assets to demonstrate its stewardship and to provide assurance to the citizens of the city that the use of public funds entrusted to their government has been fully and properly accounted for  62193 applicability a this policy is applicable to all classes of capital assets it shall be the responsibility of the mayor in consultation with the city clerk to develop procedures necessary to the implementation of this policy statement b procedures developed to implement this policy shall be binding on all employees of the city and the willful failure to follow those procedures or to carry out the intent of this policy shall constitute grounds for disciplinary action  62193 definitions a the following definitions are applicable to capital assets subject to this policy statement 1 land all real property currently in the possession of the city or acquired in the future and held in fee simple or other conditions of whole or partial ownership including leasehold interests shall constitute land holdings for purposes of this policy except as hereinafter exempted the cost or value of structures and improvements on city land whether constructed or otherwise acquired shall be separately accounted for in appropriate categories 2 improvements to land improvements to land shall constitute all nonstructure improvements to land including but not limited to such improvements as fencing sidewalks access drives outdoor seating lighting systems utility services and similar improvements with individual costs or values in excess of $250000 except as hereinafter exempted 3 structures structures represent buildings and permanently attached fixtures and equipment including but not limited to office buildings meeting halls maintenance facilities warehouses and other buildings constructed or acquired by the city with a cost or value in excess of $500000 except as hereinafter exempted 4 construction in progress construction in progress shall mean the cost or added value to date of structures and improvements to land which are incomplete but which are expected to meet the criteria established for the recording of such assets when completed 5 tangible personal property tangible personal property shall mean property consisting of fixtures and other tangible personal property of a nonconsumable nature the value of which is $20000 or more and the normal expected life of which is one year or more 6 intangible personal property intangible personal property shall for the purposes of this policy statement include the cost or value of copyrights patents and similar items which the city is licensed to use in the pursuit of its public business which licenses or permissions were acquired at a cost of more than $10000 and which licenses for periods of more than one year intangible personal property for purposes of this policy statement shall include computer software licensed to the city but shall not include depository balances or the claims on financial assets evidenced by financial instruments such as certificates of deposit notes bonds or similar evidences of indebtedness b exemptions 1 the following capital assets are specifically exempted from the provisions of this policy statement a land used by the city without charge or at nominal cost but title to which is vested in agencies of the federal state or county governments b improvements to land commonly classed as infrastructure assets typically rightofway roads utility easements docks statues park improvements and similar assets are categorized as infrastructure assets generally the publics access to and enjoyment of such assets is relatively unrestricted other than for public health and safety considerations c intangible personal property commonly accounted for as current rather than capital assets of the city examples include financial claims against banks and other depositories and investments in private or other governmental debt offerings  62193 land a all land as defined in subsection 2333a1 shall be cataloged and recorded in the public records of the city at the acquisition cost or estimated historical cost at the date of acquisition land donated to city purposes shall be valued at its fair market value at the date of acquisition b the citys public records shall include at a minimum the legal description of the property its acquisition cost or value the method of acquisition the date of acquisition if known references identifying the location of the deed or other evidence of title supporting the citys claim of ownership or use appropriate recording references to the public records of barbour county alabama or other governmental jurisdiction for the public recording of title the nature of any encumbrances of title and as appropriate the date of satisfaction of such encumbrances  62193 improvements to land a improvements to land as defined in subsection 2333a2 shall be cataloged and valued at cost or estimated historical cost at the date of acquisition improvements donated to the city shall be valued at fair market value as of the date acquired cost shall include but not be limited to engineering design architectural construction and associated landscaping costs associated with the improvements b the citys public records shall include at a minimum a description of the improvements and their locations the method of acquisition the cost or value of the improvements serial numbers for any equipment incorporated into the improvements the date of acquisition of the improvements and a notation as to their current condition the public records shall also note any encumbrances against the improvements and as appropriate the date the encumbrances were satisfied  62193 structures a structures as defined in subsection 2333a3 shall be cataloged and valued at cost or estimated historical cost at the date of acquisition structures donated to the city shall be valued at fair market value as of the date acquired cost shall include but not be limited to engineering design architectural construction and associated equipment and site improvement costs associated with the structures b the citys public records shall include at a minimum a description of the structures and their location method of acquisition the cost or value of the structures serial numbers and descriptions for any equipment incorporated into the structures the date of acquisition of the structures and a notation as to the structures current condition the public records shall also note any encumbrances against the improvements and as appropriate the date the encumbrances were satisfied  62193 construction in progress a the city clerk shall keep records by project identifying capital assets subject to recording in accordance with this policy statement in the process of construction the assets shall upon completion be transferred to the appropriate asset categories b the records shall at a minimum include descriptions of the assets under construction appropriate references to construction contracts and related cost records the date of commencement of the construction the costs incurred to date including but not limited to permitting and inspection costs architectural and engineering design costs site improvement costs construction and permanent equipment costs date of completion of the construction the city official or employee accepting the asset on behalf of the city and such other information as the city clerk may deem appropriate  62193 tangible personal property a tangible personal property as defined in subsection 2333a4 shall be recorded at cost including the amount received as credit for exchanged items or estimated historical cost if actual cost is not determinable tangible personal property items donated to the city and items constructed by city personnel shall be valued at their fair market value at the date of acquisition or construction b each item of tangible personal property as defined in subsection 2333a4 which it is practicable to identify by marking shall be marked in the manner required by the procedures promulgated by the mayor in consultation with the city clerk c the city clerk shall maintain adequate records of the citys tangible personal property which records shall contain such information as shall be required by the mayor as set forth in adopted written procedures d the city clerk shall be responsible for annually inventorying the citys tangible personal property or whenever there is a change in custodians each inventory date shall be entered on the property records the inventory shall be compared with the property records and all discrepancies shall be traced and resolved e each city department head shall be primarily responsible for the supervision and control of assigned property but may delegate to a custodian its use and immediate control and may require custody receipts a department head may assign to or withdraw from a custodian the custody of any of its property at any time  provided that if the custodian is an officer elected by the people the property may not be withdrawn from his custody without his consent each custodian shall be responsible to the department head or mayor as appropriate for the safekeeping and proper use of the property entrusted to his care  62193 intangible assets a intangible assets as defined in subsection 2333a5 shall be recorded at cost or estimated historical cost if the actual cost is not determinable the value of the assets purchased by a governmental type fund shall not be amortized  however when the use of the intangible asset is discontinued the value shall be removed from the citys general fixed asset accounting records b licensed intangible assets shall be used solely for the citys public purposes and the unauthorized use copying or similar conversion of licensed material to other uses shall be grounds for disciplinary action c the citys public records shall contain at a minimum a description of the rights licensed to the city the name and proprietary owner of any computer software the acquired the cost or other value the locations of use including the serial numbers of machines in which installed and the location of the licensing agreement  62193 renovations and repairs a renovation and repair costs shall not be capitalized unless the affected structures and improvements to land are 1 substantially expanded in capacity or the basic construction status of the structure or improvement changes  or 2 the life of the structure or improvement is substantially extended and 3 the original costs of the structural elements or improvements replaced can be removed from the recorded value of the structures or improvements  62193 property acquisition a it is the intent of the city council that the following procedures will be observed when acquiring capital assets 1 land purchases of land must be approved by the city council after appropriate review of the proposed acquisition by the city attorney land acquisitions the exchange of city property or any combination thereof may be made only after securing an independent appraisal from a qualified appraiser of the property to be acquired and if applicable the property to be exchanged 2 structures and improvements to land decisions to acquire structures and other improvements shall for existing improvements be based on competent written independent appraisals when the cost exceeds $1000000 acquisitions of existing structures and improvements valued at less than $1000000 shall be based on determinations of value compiled by the city engineer or city clerk as appropriate procurement of acquisitions to be constructed shall be based on competitive bids to the greatest extent practicable 3 tangible personal property whenever acquiring tangible personal property the mayor may pay the purchase price in full or may exchange similar property with the seller as a tradein and apply the exchange allowance to the cost of the property acquired if whenever acquiring property the mayor may best serve the public interest of the city by outright sale of the property to be replaced rather than by exchange as a tradein he may make the sale in the manner otherwise prescribed in this policy statement for the disposal of property  62193 disposition of property a all dispositions of property belonging to the city must be approved by the city council the determination of property to be disposed of by the city council shall be at the election of the city council in the reasonable exercise of its discretion b authority for the disposal of property shall be recorded in the minutes of the city the disposal of tangible personal property shall be recorded in the records required by that section c the minimum procedures for disposing of property in the following categories shall be as follows 1 land the city council in open meeting may determine that certain land is surplus to the citys needs or should be exchanged for other land in the best interests of the city land so identified may be disposed of bids auction to the highest bidder land shall be exchanged or disposed of only after securing an independent appraisal from a qualified appraiser such appraisal shall become a public record of the city 2 other tangible property the city council shall have discretion to classify as surplus any of its property which property is not otherwise lawfully disposed of that is obsolete or the continued use of which is uneconomical or inefficient or which serves no useful function a within the reasonable exercise of its discretion and having consideration for the best interest of the city the value and condition of property classified as surplus and the probability of such property being desired by the prospective bidders to whom offered the city council first shall offer surplus property to other governmental units in the county if no acceptable offer is received from a governmental unit the property may be disposed of by competitive bid or by public auction such offer shall disclose the value and condition of the property b property the value of which the city council estimates to be between $20000 and $99999 shall be sold only to the highest responsible bidder after a request for at least three bids or by public auction any sale of property the value of which the city council estimates to be $100000 or more shall be sold only to the highest responsible bidder or by public auction after publication of notice not less than one week nor more than two weeks prior to sale in a newspaper having a general circulation in the county and in additional newspapers if in the judgment of the city council the best interests of the city will be better served by the additional notices c if the property is without commercial value it may be donated destroyed or abandoned  62193 accounting principles a it is the intent of city council that the public records of the citys capital assets provide an adequate basis for financial reporting purposes and for identifying insurable city capital assets b to carry out its intent city council herewith adopts those generally accepted principles promulgated by the government accounting standards board as the accepted methodology for accounting and reporting on the citys capital assets these accounting principles are currently defined in the codification of governmental accounting and financial reporting standards as of july 199 published by the governmental accounting standards board  62193 secs 23442360 the city rules and regulations the following regulations shall be in effect in the district 1 outside consumption of alcoholic beverages permittedconditions  a within the district the alabama alcoholic beverage control board may issue an entertainment district designation for any onpremises retail alcohol beverage license which allows the licensee to sell alcohol beverages for consumption on the licensed premises patrons may not exit licensed premises with more than one open container of alcoholic beverages all alcoholic beverages sold for consumption outside the licensed premises shall be contained in a paper or plastic container that bears the commercially printed name andor logo of the designated licensee the event sponsors main street eufaula inc the district or any combination of the above b no licensee shall allow a person to exit such licensed premises with more than one such open approved container and and it shall be unlawful for any person to exit such licensed premises with more than one such open approved container c during special events during special events the district or a portion thereof shall be open for public possession and consumption of alcoholic beverages anywhere within the confines of the district or a portion of the district as provided in the permit public possession and consumption of alcoholic beverages shall be allowed as provided herein on dates specified on an assembly permit lawfully issued by the city for events approved by main street eufaula inc a request for an assembly permit for events where public possession and consumption of alcohol within the district is to be considered must include all the information required by section 8273 of the eufaula ordinances and be submitted to eufaula main street inc for approval prior to consideration by the city eufaula main street inc may establish a fee for review and processing applications for permits events that include such activities as the sale of alcoholic beverages outside of licensed premises street closures entertainment using amplified sound or other regulated activities must comply with all laws ordinances or regulations governing such activities applications for such assemblies or special events shall be forwarded by the city clerk to the chief of police the fire chief city planner or their respective designees for review prior to final approval by the city d outdoor dining areas the district shall be open for public possession and consumption of alcoholic beverages between the hours of  am to  pm monday only in a licensees outdoor dining areas that are situated on a sidewalk or other rightofway where the licensee has a rightofway use agreement with the city of eufaula e citysponsored opening of the district at any time and from time to time the city may elect to sponsor the opening of all or a portion of the district 2 right to enter restricted  during any such special event patrons or guests of a licensee with an entertainment district designation may exit that licensees licensed premises with one open container of alcoholic beverage in an approved container and consume such alcoholic beverage anywhere within the confines of the district but may not enter another licensed premises with an open container of alcoholic beverages acquired elsewhere 3 all applicable laws in effect  a licensee who is within the district shall comply with all laws rules and regulations which govern its license type 4 size limited to 16 ounces  no container in which an alcoholic beverage is dispensed and removed from the licensed premises shall exceed 16 fluid ounces in size no person shall be in possession of any above prescribed alcoholic beverage container which exceeds 16 fluid ounces in size on the streets and sidewalks in parks or in other public places within the defined district 5 drinking from can bottle or glass is prohibited  it shall be unlawful for any person within the confines of the district to drink or attempt to drink any alcoholic beverage from a can bottle or glass or to possess in an open can bottle or glass any alcoholic beverage on the streets sidewalks rightsofway and parking lots whether public or private  other than as duly licensed by the state of alabama and the city it shall also be unlawful for any person within the confines of the district to drink or attempt to drink any alcoholic beverage on the streets sidewalks rightsofway and parking lots whether public or private from a container other than an approved container 6 open container laws applicable  open container laws of the state of alabama and the city of eufaula still govern to the extent that the respective provisions are not strictly modified by either section 283a171 of the alabama 197 section 283a201 of the alabama 1975 or the provisions of this chapter 7 hours for special events  special events permitted within the district shall only be allowed between the hours of  am to  pm monday 8 consumption of alcoholic beverages in a motor vehicle prohibited  it shall be unlawful for any person to consume any alcoholic beverages in a motor vehicle parked or in motion within the district with the exception of a common carrier vehicle licensed by the board to serve alcoholic beverages 9 refill prohibited  it shall be unlawful for any person to refill a container from a licensed premises with alcoholic beverages not purchased at a licensed premises within the district it shall be unlawful for any person to reuse or to knowingly allow the reuse of an approved container for an alcoholic beverage and nothing in this chapter shall be construed to authorize the same 10 alcoholic beverage from another licensed premises prohibited  it shall be unlawful for any person to enter a licensed premises with alcoholic beverages acquired at another licensed premises or outside the district 11 underage drinking prohibited  nothing in this chapter shall be construed to authorize any person to violate the state and citys laws against underage drinking 12 churches and excluded areas  no church shall be considered part of the district any public building facility garage or parking lot that is posted with signage at each entrance or in conspicuous places that no open containers of alcoholic beverages are allowed on the premises shall be excluded from the district property privately owned or controlled that is posted with signage at each entrance or in conspicuous places that no open containers of alcoholic beverages are allowed on the premises shall also be excluded  i 8112014   violations any violation of any provision of chapter shall be a misdemeanor punishable by a fine of not less than $10000 nor more than $100000 per violation to which at the discretion of the court or judge trying the case may add imprisonment or a sentence to hard labor for not more than three months or may be punished by both such fine and imprisonment the city council may also consider suspension or revocation of the business license of any licensee who violates any provision of this chapter  i 8112014 signage boundary maps of the district with the hours of operation of the district shall be clearly marked with fixed signage at all entrancesexits of licensed premises within the district signs shall indicate the prohibition of removing beverages from the district the boundary of the district shall be clearly marked with signs for pedestrians entering the district during special events displaying the hours of operation and indicating the prohibition on removing alcoholic beverages from the area  i 8112014 temporary closure of the district at any time and from time to time the chief of police or his designee shall have the authority to temporarily close the district or portions of the district which includes authority to require individuals to disperse from the area should he in his sole discretion determine it is appropriate to do so in order to protect the public health safety or general welfare the district shall remain closed until the chief of police or his designee allows the district to be reopened the city shall not be responsible for any costs incurred by any person or business as a result of the closing  i 8112014 amendments the city council may amend modify or revoke the designation of any area as an entertainment district upon finding that the operation of the district has become a nuisance or is otherwise not being operated in the best public interest including lack of adequate security the city council may also require that the licensees located within the district provide additional security at their own expense nothing in this chapter shall be construed to create any right or entitlement to entertainment district designation  i immediately deposited in substantial flyproof containers all such collections may be kept stored in substantial flyproof containers for a continuous period of two weeks from date of collection sawdust six inches underground or by spreading the manure and other material thinly upon the surface of the ground at some place distant from human habitation or any place where animals are kept so that the owner or handler immediate presence for the purpose of this article shall be defined as a radius of 50 feet from the owner running at large means any animal which is not controlled by any adequate upon the property of the owner or upon property which the owner has permission for the dog to be on any words not specifically defined herein shall have their usual and common meanings a dog shall not be deemed to be running at large if any of the following apply 1 the dog is confined in a building or fenced pen or yard on its owners property or on the property of another person with the other persons consent 2 the dog is leashed and securely tied on its owners property or on the property of another person with the other owners consent in such position that the dog cannot gain access to public property or other private property 3 the dog whether on leash or not is under the immediate and effective control of a responsible person  provided that the dog shall not be considered under restraint if it is on the property of a person other than its owner without the consent of the other person 4 the dog though not meeting any of the conditions stated in 1 2 and 3 above is in a peaceful attitude on the property of its owner and is wearing license and vaccination tags as prescribed in section 1483 below  provided that the dog shall not be considered under restraint in this case if the dog was chased to its owners property by the animal control officer or other agent of the city or if the dog is the subject of an outstanding written complaint duly filed with the police division andor municipal court the dog shall not be considered under restraint for purposes of this section during sweep periods as described in section 14825 and 1484c 5 sweep periods are periods designated by the chief of police or the chiefs designee with prior notification being given to the mayor and city council during which all dogs must be kept leased when not in a private building fenced in run or fenced yard these periods shall be instituted as necessary to ensure that all stray dogs may more easily be apprehended sweep periods shall not be longer than seven days in duration and shall not be of greater frequency than four times in any calendar year any dog apprehended during sweep periods not under leash restraint or in a private building fenced run or fenced yard shall be subject to the provisions of section 1495 of this article tethering or chaining  these terms are commonly defined as fastening a dog to a stationary object or stake with a chain rope or other such device that is attached to the dogs collar this is often used as the sole means of keeping the animal restrained and under control it does not refer to the periods when an animal is being walked on a leash  101893  ii 7201   a  tethering and chaining a dogs and small animals are prohibited from being tethered or chained to a stationary or fixed point dogs and small animals are allowed to be confined by a trolley system provided the owner is on the premises and certain requirements are met 1 no owner keeper harborer or maintainer of a dog may tether fasten chain or tie a dog to any permanent or temporary structure  any post attached to the ground or to any weight designed to restrict the dogs freedom of movement to a limited area of space 2 dogs and small animals may be restrained by a trolley system or a tether attached to a pulley on a cable run provided that the owner is on the premises and the following conditions are met a only one dog or small animal may be tethered to each cable run b the tether must be attached to a properly fitting collar or harness worn by the dog or small animal with enough room between the collar and the animals throat two fingers may fit choke collars and pinch collars are strictly prohibited for purposes of tethering a dog or small animal to a cable run the use of any collar too small for the size and age of the animal or by any rope chain or cord directly attached to the animals neck is prohibited c there must be a swivel on both ends of the tether to minimize tangling of the tether d the tether and cable run must be of adequate size and strength to effectively restrain the dog or small animal the size and weight of the tether must not be excessive as determined by the enforcement officer considering the age size and health of the dog in general the use of a tether that exceeds 25 percent of the body weight of the dog or small animal is prohibited e the cable run must be at least 15 feet in length and mounted at least four feet and no more than seven feet above ground level f the length of the tether from the cable run to the animals collar should allow access to the maximum available exercise area and should allow continuous access to food water and shelter g in no case shall it be permitted that a dog or small animal be confined so as to be forced to stand sit or lie in its own excrement or on ground that is not well drained h the trolley system must be of appropriate configuration to confine the dog or small animal to the owners property to prevent the tether from extending over an object or an edge that could result in injury or strangulation of the dog or small animal and to prevent the tether from becoming entangled with other objects or animals i dogs and small animals shall not be confined use of a trolley system between the hours of  pm and  am j unsterilized female dogs shall not be tethered attached to a trolley or cable run unless monitored by a competent adult for the duration of such tethering k dogs and small animals should never be tethered during natural disasters such as floods fires tornadoes blizzards or other severe weather  rabies vaccinations  rabies vaccination tag required a every person who owns harbors or keeps or maintains a dog or cat over the age of four 4 months shall secure on an annual basis a rabies vaccination for such animal including the proper certificate and tag from a licensed veterinarian as long as the dog or cat is within the city b each dog over the age of four months shall wear a substantial durable collar or harness to which the vaccination tag shall be attached provided however that this requirement is exempted while such dog is confined to the property of the owner and provided further the owner shall be required to produce evidence of a rabies vaccination tag upon request of the aco it shall be unlawful to attach such tag by wire rope or by any inhumane means no person shall remove the collar or vaccination tag from any animal without the consent of the owner it shall be a defense to any prosecution under this section for any dog owner to produce a written letter from a veterinarian stating that due to the size and shape of any properly vaccinated dog a collar or harness will not stay on the particular dog without running the risk of undue injury to the dog or if it can be shown that such dog routinely wears a collar but the owner is unaware that the collar is off of the dog c cats are not required to wear the rabies vaccination tag if the rabies vaccination tag is not worn the owner shall be required to produce evidence of the rabies vaccination tag upon request of the aco d it shall be unlawful for any person to permit or allow any dog or cat in his charge or control to wear a rabies vaccination tag issued for a different animal  101893   82195   animals at large a constant physical control required a dog owner shall keep his or her dog under physical control at all times any dog
